After losing our beloved older female Husky, we adopted a two-year female Husky from the animal shelter.  After bringing her home, the sweet dog that we met at the animal shelter suddenly became a holy terror.  Not only was she driving our older male Husky crazy, she was biting and chewing on everything including us.  After three weeks of canine craziness, we contacted K-9 Companions and immediately enrolled Sierra in the three-week Boot Camp. < text>
I have a new German Shepherd puppy that was in serious need of basic training because of his extremely high energy. I live alone which made the desire to have him under control even more of a necessity. When he was too young to get a rabies shot (14 weeks old) I found a private trainer that would accept him for 3 week basic obedience and keep him separate from any other dogs (full shots are a necessary requirement). That did help some and gave him a decent head start, but the results after a lot of $$ and 3 weeks away from my new puppy were not everything that is advertised, which is generally the same for most puppy ‚Äúboot camps‚Äù. When he was a couple months older with all of his shots and much more work with him on my own at home, I decided to look for a more comprehensive training facility and was recommended K-9 Companions from somebody at the doggie day care he goes to. When I took him in for evaluation I anticipated that he would be going to the intermediate/off leash, 2nd level program. He was way ahead of the game from a first timer but not up to the standards K-9 Companions expects after their 1st level of obedience. He had to brush up and advance his basic training (sit, stay, heel, down, come, no, off...) for one week and was able to move on to the next level for the next 2 weeks. He came back a different dog! Still as sweet and playful as he had been from day 1, but he obeyed everything he was taught as if he was having fun doing it. When I take him for walks or anyone comes to the house, every single person who meets him can‚Äôt believe how well behaved he is for such an energetic puppy. I have even recommended to several people that they take their misbehaving or untrained adult dogs to K-9 Companions for at least basic obedience. I am certain that it has done as much for my dog‚Äôs quality of life as it has for my own enjoyment of him, and believe that would be true for any dog owner/parent. After a couple more months at home with me, he does SO well and enjoys working on everything he has learned so much, I decided to put him through more advanced training. I had already taken him back for short boarding and brush up training and he absolutely loves the staff, as they do him. No separation anxiety at all (I may have a little:) and he was genuinely excited to be back. There was no hesitation at all as the quality of the facility and the care he is given there is top notch. In researching dog training facilities the first thing reviewers and experts say is to do your homework on the facility, they are not all equal. I am 100% comfortable knowing my baby is in great hands at K-9 companions. He is currently there as I‚Äôm writing, going through his off-leash and advanced training. I could not recommend this facility and their staff any more than saying my dog is now on his third stay there and I know he is loving it as much as I will be when he comes home. The follow up training that is included has been invaluable more in the sense of training ME than my dog. He knows exactly what to do, it‚Äôs up to me to know how to properly communicate with positive reinforcement. This training is worth every penny and will pay back dividends with years of enjoyment for both you and your dog. I have owned many dogs throughout my life and never had one formally trained. I thought they were so smart (they were) but had never realized their full potential. I thought my own training that only came from years of repetition was enough. I had no idea the difference professional training would make and am now a firm believer that if anybody has the means to do it, like me they would consider it a necessity.</text>

<Rating>5</Rating><text>I think it is important for anyone considering a free consultation at K-9 Companions to understand that the reason for the consultation is to evaluate the dogs temperament and the needs of both the dog and the client. Some dogs need to see a veterinarian for medical or temperament issues due to medical issues prior to training. Some people wish to train their dogs in a manner that is as inexpensive as possible and therefore need to spend more time being involved in the training themselves (such as driving to the facility weekly) and not boarding the dog while training. Other clients prefer to have as much as possible done for them and would prefer to board the dog (costs more) and have as much of the training as possible done for them. Some dogs actually need this level of training due to a lack of socialization or due to them being fearful or aggressive. There is no way that a trainer can tell an owner over the phone what the dog is going to need. This is why the consultation is FREE. The training prescribed could be as little as a (local) in home lesson for $100.00. It could be lessons at the facility for $250-$495. The client might want lessons done in their home (at a higher cost) or they might want the Mercedes of dog training which involves the dog staying (boarding) at the facility, followed by lesson/s in their home and a number of follow up lessons over the next year at the facility.< /text>< pics>

< text>
I read all the reviews about k-9 companions and I do not believe what everyone has to say about this place.  I decided to take my puppy in for puppy training as he is a handful. < Text>
My family and I were in the process of moving into a new home in Lake Arrowhead and decided that our 10 month old Chesapeak Bay Retriever, Hank, needed formal training. We met with Dianne for our consultation and she assured me when Hank was done with boot camp that he would be an extremely well behaved young pup.We dropped Hank off August 2 and would be picking him up on August 23rd.

9 days into doggy training (August 11th), I received 4 back to back phone calls from a blocked number. I had my wife call and K9 Companions said Hank wasn't looking well so they took him to the vet. About an hour after they brought him back from the vet, they called saying we needed to pick him up immediately and take him to our vet. When we picked Hank up, he couldn't stand up and could barely lift his head. I had to carry him. You could tell he was extremely ill.

I took him to our local vet and the Dr took one look at Hank and said this is extremely concerning. He did X-rays and ran a parvo test. Hank came back negative for parvo and didn't have any foreign bodies lodged in his stomach but he had fluid in his lungs and was running a high fever. The vet told me, if I do not take Hank to the 24/7 emergency vet in Ontario, that Hank would not make it through the night.

I rushed Hank down the mountain and he was admitted immediately on the spot. The vet told me that Hank was in extremely rough shape and there is a chance he will not see the following morning.

Hank spent 5 days at the emergency vet with 24/7 care. Fortunately, he pulled through. He contracted a viral infection, a bacterial infection, para influenza and developed and pneumonia. Our total medical bills were over $6,000. The vet said he contracted it from this place.

K9 Companion assured us that they have never seen a case like this and that there have been no other cases of dogs getting this sick. The K9 companion staff seemed to be concerned about Hank the entire time, until it was time to talk about the bill. Dianne, the manager, was extremely worried about Hank and genuinely cared about Hanks health. She presented all the findings and bills to the owner. The owner, Laura said, there will be no reimbursement for Hanks medical bills.

K9 Companions is responsible for almost killing my dog and burying me in a financial hole. My wife stays at home with our 16 month old son. I am the sole provider. I am an Operation Enduring Freedom Veteran and still serve in the military. Our bills are worth two months of pay and we still have to take Hank in to be checked frequently to make sure his lungs have 100% recovered.

Once Hank returned home we had multiple vet visits and required attention at all times from my wife. We had to cancel a family vacation that was planned due to this nightmare. After 4 weeks of being on 3 different types of medication, having to doing breathing treatments, under constant supervision and having to be extremely careful with him, our puppy is starting to act like himself again. We are so thankful for the 24 hour Vet that saved our dogs life.

Bottom line is, do not take your dog here unless you want to deal with what we have dealt with. Morality has taken a back seat to these people and all they care about are pure profits.

***I have been in contact with another dog owner that had a similar experience as us. If you have had something similar to this, please get into contact with us!***</Text>

<review>So I bought this F6B Honda 2 months ago from this store, it took a bit of negotiating , but in the end all was well and I drove off a happy customer.
I went to this store based upon my buddy having bought his there as well and was happy with the way they treated him.

Now comes the important stuff, since many stores have pleasant people working there to a greater degree,good inventory, selection, waiting lounges, free coffee, etc, etc, this is not what set stores apart from each other,and although important to some, for me the answer is the service after they have your money and what kind of service you gonna get in return for your time and money.

In my case I must say that I'm overly impressed by the way this store took care of business.

I developed two minor warranty issues with my plastic covers on the bike, went in to see the service   tech David who took a look of the issue at hand, took some pictures, and said he would contact Honda on the parts, and advise me on the warranty clause.

Two days later I was contacted by Mo in the parts department, who stated that my parts were there, Honda was going to cover the items, and whenever I was ready, to come on in for the install of the parts.

Now this is service, I did not have to hound them down, they contacted me, as it should have and gave me the option for the install time and date.

But it gets better, and no I do not get paid for writing this review.

The mechanic Dean who did this repair work was on the money,very professional,and knowledgeable and took time to explain the procedure .

This visit and repair was one of the best I have had, and I been around the block (riding M/C for 40 yrs) and have seen at least 3 other Honda shops for various state of repairs, but would not go back to any of them, for that there was always something what caused me to be upset, like they did not tighten the screws, forgot something, missing a part, etc, etc.

Anyhow I gladly drive the 80 miles one way to get my MC serviced here, and hope you will have as good fortune as I had.< /review>< pics>

<Review>DON'T WASTE YOUR TIME HERE.

I decided to check out the new Honda dealership since in the past I had to go out to Santa Monica or Irvine to check out new Honda motorcycles. Well, bottom line is, I will not be returning to this dealership. They wasted enough of my time today so I won't let them waste more by spending a long time on this review.

I stopped in on a Tuesday, spoke with the manager Mr. Cavenagh (Greg, I think) and said I was interested in trading in my 2012 Kawasaki Vulcan 900 Custom for a 2015 Honda Fury, he said that would be great and I could come in with my bike any day and do a test ride and they could check out the trade. So i came in 2 days later with my bike, the sales person, Eric, whom I had been dealing with on the phone earlier in the day setting up the demo ride with, came out, checked out the bike, said it was great and had me turn it on, rev, etc. So then we go talk numbers, they offer me a fair enough amount for my trade, we come to an agreement on price after about an hour, which includes the usual way over invoice markup and whatnot, and they had the classic bait and switch (listed for $1000 less on their website) and make it sound like they are doing me a big favor by honoring...their own price they had listed... SO, Then comes the test ride to make sure I enjoy the bike (I have 4 bikes at the moment and am very particular about what I want in a new bike)

Eric says he doesn't have a demo bike for the Fury so it will be about and hour while they set one up so I can demo it. After some more waiting he comes back and says that  I can only demo ride if its sold to me (not much of a demo...if I own it) and also, they did not want to take my bike as a trade because its a Kawasaki and they are Honda only and don't really have the ability to take a non-honda in a trade. THIS is what made me really angry, the whole time they knew what bike I was interested in trading. They knew damn well it was not a Honda, and it's in great condition so that wasn't an issue (garage kept, only 3k miles, etc) Good enough condition that after checking it out they had offered me a good enough trade in value for us to advance to the next hour or so of negotiation. He said it was management that was to blame, yet when i spoke to general manager originally and set it all up, it was no issue at all. Nor is it an issue at any other dealership, even brand exclusive ones. Also, I should mention they have used NON HONDA bikes already on their website listed under pre-owned inventory.

So they literally wasted about 3 hours of my only day off (not to mention some gas money going over there again) What really pisses me off is that they were about to run my credit for financing, knowing they were just going to not take the trade and still try to sell me the Fury. Hoping I would just buy it anyways?

I'm still interested in the Fury, so I guess I will have to drive out to Mission Motorsports in Irvine (They have a great staff and no BS) What a disappointment though.

Totally a waste of time and energy for nothing.<//Review>< Pics>

< Review>
We are not very familiar with the resorts in Tahoe, but our experience at this one was very good.
Edgelake has a good size beach right on the lake that is especially good for families looking to spread out, with lots of sand for the kids. They also had the only two story boat dock pier that I've ever seen. Very nice pool area too.
They are timeshare condos, and are available at a discount directly from the owners. You have to go to websites like VRBO to accomplish this.< /Review>

We've been staying here for years and would give all of those visits a FIVE STAR... always staying in #12 or #14.  This year we were place in #19 and for that reason I would give this stay only a ONE STAR.  The location of #19 is next to the office and the maintenance supply room.  Absolutely NO privacy as people walked by constantly, staring into our room.  The room was dark so at times we opened the front door and people would just walk in mistaken our room for a community room.  We had no personal chairs outside our room like the other rooms.  The roar of the street at night was terrible, you had to keep your window closed otherwise you were up all night.  We've never had these issues before, ever... always amazing and refreshed so my comments are just directed toward this unit location only.  We were pleased to see the updates to the property and as always other tenants were a pleasure to talk to each day and night.<//text>

<Rating>5</Rating>< Text>
Beautiful hike, but get there early if you want a good parking spot. The trail gets a little crowded in the afternoon since you come back on the same trail, but take your time exploring the creek and Cascade Falls, there are plenty of little hidden gems all around. Also bring some lunch as there are plenty of places to hang out in the shade and enjoy the views while you eat.<//Text>

< Text>
Recommend for sunrise/sunset hike as it's a short 3/4mi in and another 3/4mi out. Seems heavily tracked although I've only seen three people out there for my sunset hike. My favorite part was hanging out on a rock and sitting there with some folks but definitely go to the waterfall.

About the hike, it's not strenuous. Incline is steady. GOOD FOR KIDS. Be mindful driving to the trailhead. You drive through a campsite before reaching the parking lot.< /Text>

< review>
Was here and the views were amazing. The waterfall thats there doesn't actually run year round or much so it was disappointing to hike 40ish mintues to no waterfall.
However dont let that discourage you from going. Its breath taking.
What I would say though is make sure to use the restroom before driving in and to cool it on the water.
The restrooms are horrible. As in if I were to post a picture of it on here it would make you sick.
Let's just leave it at that.</review>

<Review>Cascade Falls was amazing. Huge water fall! (Hiked it end of June on a Monday). Took two kids 8 and 11 and they had a blast. Lots of boulders and rocks along the way, very fun!  This is an easy to moderate hike. Bring a snack or lunch to eat at the falls (trail ends above the falls, you see them as you hike in and out). 2 miles round trip.  Started at the trailhead 10 am done by Noon. Plenty of time left in the day to hit another site or activity. Parking is FREE but very small, go early.< /Review>< Pictures>

<review>Unparalleled views. Glad I went.  Even happier that I didn't give myself a heart attack.  Seriously, this trail is no joke!   Grades are steep and consistent ALL the way up.  Desolation Trail, you'd think the name would have given me a clue!!
Anyway, I am 55 years old and sedintary.   There was a woman up there looking for her dog.  She had already gone up and down the trail, and then JOGGED back up calling for her dog.  Wow,  she was a beast!!!!  So it's all relative to your fitness level.  Take water, for sure.   I wish I had sprayed bug repellent on my arms beforehand.  Otherwise, no regrets.  We went late in the day, no trouble parking or crowds. Nice!</review><pictures>None< /pictures><Response>None<//Response>< GmapID>

< text>
I have been fortunate enough to have Dr. Osias as my Optometrist for a number of years.  Dr. Osias is like an old friend, and he treats me as such, he knows about my preexisting conditions and always keeps a watchful eye on my eye's and eye wear.
Normally, I see Dr. Osias for my annual eye exam, however this year I ran into a bit of trouble with my Primary Physicians request that I get an eye screening at Kaiser.  Kaiser "found" a problem with my eyes with the pictures they took. Not only did this put a good scare into me it also added a lot of stress to my world.
Dr. Osias was happy to recheck my eyes, and run a new Optomap series of images on my eyes even though I had a series of pics done in February at my annual check up.  Dr. Osias worked with me to figure out what Kaiser had likely seen. It turned out Dr. Osias had already seen the issue and was watching it. He collected data and drafted a note for the people at Kaiser, explaining his findings and the promise that IF my eye's developed a problem he would without hesitation direct me to the right people to get any corrective action taken.
I have loyalty to Dr. Osias, that only comes with years of working together, trust and mutual respect.
Primary Eyecare has been there for me when i was a cash paying customer as well as when I had insurance.  They have always tried to work with me to save money, and they are flexible in working around my schedule.
I would and will recommend Dr. Osias without any hesitation.<//text>

<Text>I've been going there for over 25 years when they had the old office in San Lorenzo. They had excellent customer service and great staff. However, for the past 3-5 years it has gone downhill. All of the friendly and courteous staff is gone. I walk in for an adjustment and they say everything has to be done my appointment. I can understand if they are busy, but sometimes it'll be only myself sitting in the loby. I always paid cash and did not use my insurance because when you pay with cash they give you a two year warranty on your lenses and frames. I have used their services more then once in two years. All of a sudden, if you pay cash you only get one time exchange. Also, if you pay cash you only one exchange in two years. I asked to speak to the supervisor and she tells me this has always been their policy. I told that you have did this before where you exchange it for me past practice, and she said no. I told her to look at my file so she could see it. I asked to speak to the owner.  I was told she would replay the message and get back to me in a week, which he never did. I usually spend between $500-800 on a single pair of glasses every year at their office for my 3 kids and I, so I expect when there is a deep scratch or a problem with the frame they'll honor their product and their warrant.
